    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1129307101" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1129307101" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1129307101?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=assassins">assassins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1129307101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6276749342023762667"><b>My heart is split in two.</b><br/><b>
  <blockquote>“Once upon a time, in a land long since burned to ash, there lived a young princess who loved her kingdom …” </blockquote>
</b><br/>But this story is not only about the young princess. It's the story of a <b>white-haired queen</b> of a divided people, and the warmth that eventually melted her cold heart. It's the story of a <b>tortured king</b>, a king who was drowning in self-loathing and whose soul was darkened by demons and grief but the light within could not be extinguished. The story of a <b>dark and</b></span>
  <span id="freeText6276749342023762667" style="display:none"><b>My heart is split in two.</b><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Once upon a time, in a land long since burned to ash, there lived a young princess who loved her kingdom …” </blockquote>
</b><br>But this story is not only about the young princess. It's the story of a <b>white-haired queen</b> of a divided people, and the warmth that eventually melted her cold heart. It's the story of a <b>tortured king</b>, a king who was drowning in self-loathing and whose soul was darkened by demons and grief but the light within could not be extinguished. The story of a <b>dark and brooding warrior</b> and the <b>quiet, quick-witted mortal</b> who gave him a reason to fight; a <b>golden prince</b> whose love for his kingdom led him to unspeakable bloodshed and loss; a <b>resilient shape-shifter</b> who gave everything for her new home; a <b>forsaken lord</b> that emerged from the pit of despair and disability thanks to a <b>determined young woman</b> who healed him in more than one ways.<br>It is the story of pirates and assassins, kings and queens, Fae, demons and mortals, of different people who were united by one common goal.<br><i>A better world.</i><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Live, Manon. Live.” </blockquote>
</b><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33590260.Kingdom_of_Ash__Throne_of_Glass___7_" title="Kingdom of Ash (Throne of Glass, #7) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Kingdom of Ash</a> was <b>
  <i>powerful</i>
</b>.<br><b>
  <i>Bewitching.</i>
</b><br><b>
  <i>Gut-wrenching. </i>
</b><br>It was a sweeping conclusion, extremely <b>brutal</b> but also <b>a maelstrom of feelings, magic, precious laughter, camaraderie, friendship and love.</b> I savored the moments I found myself shaking, due to fear, sorrow or wonder; I craved the parts that gave me goosebumps, and the ones that made my chest swell. But even though <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33590260.Kingdom_of_Ash__Throne_of_Glass___7_" title="Kingdom of Ash (Throne of Glass, #7) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Kingdom of Ash</a> wrapped up everything, even though I was bestowed with <b>glorious, gritty battles and heart-warming romances</b>, I ended up wanting something more. <i>Wanting more from a 1,000 pages book</i>. And that's where I knew that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33590260.Kingdom_of_Ash__Throne_of_Glass___7_" title="Kingdom of Ash (Throne of Glass, #7) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Kingdom of Ash</a> was not my favorite instalment of the series.<br><br>And do you know why? <b>Because of Sarah playing favorites.</b><br><i>Again.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467419776ra/19591013.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When it comes to Aelin and Rowan, I feel that Sarah's writing is extremely <b>forced</b>. That <b>she tries too hard to convince</b>, to convey the message that Aelin is so amazing and powerful and worshipped, that she and Rowan are the perfect couple everyone admires and acknowledges their awesomeness. Everything about them was devoid of feeling, I could practically hear Sarah chanting <i>“see how great they are love them love them love them love them LOVE THEM DARN IT”</i> and the truth is, I couldn't. I got tired of reading the words <i>mate</i> and <i>court</i> so many times, as if Rowan and her friends had no names or something else to define them other than their relationship with Aelin. To be honest, Aelin and Rowan and the <b>plastic, strained representation</b> of their bond and Aelin's awesomeness led me to rate it with four stars.<br><br>In addition, a notion I couldn't shake was how <b>unceremonious some scenes or revelations could be</b>. In part it's my own fault, since for the life of me I couldn't remember the majority of the events that happened in the previous books (with the exception of the scorching scenes between Dorian and Manon because those are <i>forever</i> imprinted in my dysfunctional and selective memory), but knowing Sarah's talent, I do believe she could have done better. <br><br>However, when it came to the rest of the characters, it felt that Sarah <b>let go of her obsession, and that words poured effortlessly from her soul</b>. Her writing was genuine, fluid, and rattled me to the core. I shed oceans of tears for secondary characters and their sacrifices, I literally choked on them, soaked the pages with evidence of my mourning and heartache. My skin tingled whenever Elide and Lorcan (whose treating was so, so unfair) shared a precious moment, when Nesryn and Sartaq (whose page time was criminally limited because apparently endless and strained banters between Aelin and her court were more important) fought alongside for a nation that was not their own. <br><br>I did not read this series for Aelin and Rowan. There were other characters who deserved my love, respect, every star in the freaking sky, and once again, <b>the only queen I bow to, the only queen I pledge my loyalty to, is Manon Blackbeak.</b><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Be the bridge, be the light. When iron melts, when flowers spring from fields of blood - let the land be witness, and return home.” </blockquote>
</b><br>Manon has <b>one of the most gripping storylines</b>, and the development of the bloodthirsty, cunning witch is something to behold. She crossed skies and kingdoms, searched for her identity and her future in a world that marked her as a monster, a killer and nothing more. But with iron teeth and iron nails she carved her own place, she managed to open her heart bit by bit, and embraced feelings long forgotten.<br><b>
  <blockquote>“Who do you wish to be?” </blockquote>
</b><br>Dorian Havilliard, the king of Adarlan, had a similar self-discovery arc. Gone is the carefree, flirting prince who brushed aside his responsibilities towards his now broken kingdom. He got harsher, manipulative and self-destructive, but was also guided by a fiery need to make things right, no matter the cost. I am proud of Dorian. <s>I'm going to marry Dorian</s><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498534015ra/23134676.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Let’s make this a fight worthy of a song.” </blockquote>
</b><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33590260.Kingdom_of_Ash__Throne_of_Glass___7_" title="Kingdom of Ash (Throne of Glass, #7) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Kingdom of Ash</a> was a book I was waiting for years. It was <b>bloody, emotional, sizzling, truly worthy of a song</b>; the majority of characters have scored a permanent place in my ever-loving fangirl heart. Parting with them hurts emotionally and physically, and I will always cherish this marvel of a series. My only complaint that dampened to a degree this reading experience is that, knowing the sheer magnitude that Sarah is capable of (hello <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28260587.Empire_of_Storms__Throne_of_Glass___5_" title="Empire of Storms (Throne of Glass, #5) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Empire of Storms</a>), <b>she could do justice to all of her characters, and not only to her favorite ones</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6276749342023762667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer16960159206935266186"><b>3.75 - 4 Stars</b><br/><br/>All things considered, I enjoyed this book and series a great deal. <br/><br/>As the conclusion to a pretty popular and lengthy series, it had a lot riding on its massive 980 page shoulders...and a LOT of uber-emotional fangirls and boys to avoid disappointing, let's be real. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548877228ra/26992357.gif' width='437' height='246' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Overall I thought Maas did a pretty decent job of it...<br/><br/>...even with all the filler, all the battles, ALL the traveling to and fro...all the <i>unnecessary</i>...<br/><br/>...until about page 770 or so. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548877228ra/26992358.gif' width='450' height='253' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book was...long. Probably lon</span>
  <span id="freeText16960159206935266186" style="display:none"><b>3.75 - 4 Stars</b><br><br>All things considered, I enjoyed this book and series a great deal. <br><br>As the conclusion to a pretty popular and lengthy series, it had a lot riding on its massive 980 page shoulders...and a LOT of uber-emotional fangirls and boys to avoid disappointing, let's be real. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548877228ra/26992357.gif" width="437" height="246" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall I thought Maas did a pretty decent job of it...<br><br>...even with all the filler, all the battles, ALL the traveling to and fro...all the <i>unnecessary</i>...<br><br>...until about page 770 or so. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548877228ra/26992358.gif" width="450" height="253" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book was...long. Probably longer than it needed to be, quite frankly. I saw that some people had said that - and I didn't agree, at first. I was more than perfectly content, even at page 600-something, to relish these characters and the individual storylines that made for such an epic ending for as long as it lasted. <br><br>However, at about 770-800 pages, some events in the book made me...less than enthused. With all of the build-up regarding the final "showdown" and the closing of the Wyrdgate...I was bummed with the way it all went down. <br><br>Not gonna lie, since the time it was all explained, I have wondered about the Wyrdgate...and been a little confused by it all in a way. So many gods, blood debts, and other stuff involved. And when it finally came to "the moment," as it were, I was kind of a little miffed. <br><br>Especially when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Aelin ends up losing her Fire-Bringer powers.<br><br>I'm sorry, I'm all for the ordinary being all extraordinary and all that...but I also like my "super-heroes" to have their super powers. And after so many books of Aelin finding and then learning to control this power...for her to just lose it in the end, right before the big battle? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548882712ra/26992666.gif" width="437" height="209" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548882473ra/26992653.gif" width="376" height="218" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, the whole part with Dorian...<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When he learned how to shift, I was like, cool. That's cool. But when he goes to Morath, encounters Maeve, and supposedly dupes her? I just have a hard time believing he was able to do that. <br>To overpower her and outsmart her with his magic like that after people much older and experienced with magic, i.e., Rowan and the cadre, have been unable to do so for <i>millennia</i>. And then, not to fucking kill her right then when presented the opportunity?<br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548882473ra/26992652.gif" width="245" height="245" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>And don't even get me started on the final showdown. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Once again, Maeve seems to easily take control of everyone's minds (making my point with Dorian even more ridiculous), <i>once</i> again she seems to so easily overpower them all. <br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Le sigh. <br><br>It just felt drawn out and repetitive.<br><br>Again. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548882473ra/26992652.gif" width="245" height="245" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, I was kind of left a little blue-balled by how things ended between some of the characters. But I think by then, Maas realized she was encroaching on 1000 fucking pages. And, by then, there were just SO many damned story lines, it would have been almost a whole other book to properly ties up all the loose ends in regards to everyone's story, relationships, and future. <br><br>But, whatever. <br><br>All in all, I enjoyed the majority of this book. There were some REALLY poignant moments <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Manon and her Thirteen, anyone? Holy-throat-tight-with-emotion right there, people.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And in the end, I think the idea that you can have friendships and relationships you would be willing to sacrifice your life for? Always powerful.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2351827651" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2351827651" />
    <a title="Nasom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67824881-nasom"><img alt="Nasom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520213174p2/67824881.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nasom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nasom" href="/user/show/67824881-nasom">Nasom</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2351827651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9168298681062243723"><b> My rating is between 4 and 4.5 </b><br/><br/><b> Full Review </b><br/><br/>I feel like I should get an award for finishing this big ass book. <br/><br/>Not gonna lie, I feel kinda empty now that this series has ended 😪<br/><br/><b> What I liked </b><br/>- If you looked at my reviews for the previous books, you would notice that I am not a fan of Aelin but she wasn’t bad in this. She became somewhat likeable (or maybe I just felt sorry for her)<br/><br/>- While in previous books Aelin was usually the hero and everyone pretty much worshipped her, in this, there were o</span>
  <span id="freeText9168298681062243723" style="display:none"><b> My rating is between 4 and 4.5 </b><br /><br /><b> Full Review </b><br /><br />I feel like I should get an award for finishing this big ass book. <br /><br />Not gonna lie, I feel kinda empty now that this series has ended 😪<br /><br /><b> What I liked </b><br />- If you looked at my reviews for the previous books, you would notice that I am not a fan of Aelin but she wasn’t bad in this. She became somewhat likeable (or maybe I just felt sorry for her)<br /><br />- While in previous books Aelin was usually the hero and everyone pretty much worshipped her, in this, there were other people that were heroes. Honestly, Aelin barely did anything heroic and I loved that other people were allowed to shine!!.<br /><br />- My #1 ship in this series <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Elide and Lorcan  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was just so beautiful omg!! If shipping could kill, I would have died, especially regarding the decision one of them made at the end!! <br /><br />- Another issue I had with previous books was concerning the treatment of Dorian, like he was some unimportant person. That changed here! My baby was so badass and I loved it. I just love dorian and he made me laugh a few times <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ When he changed into a girl  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and I love how compassionate he is! This guy made me feel sorry for someone that was terrible! That’s how nice he is. <br /><br />- Fenrys, The thirteen <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Poor Manon and Abraxos 😭😭  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and Yrene 💕💕<br /><br />- The friendships!! My fave friendship in this had to be Fenrys and Aelin! Who would have thought?? I just loved their bond! And no one can forget the most loyal friendship, the thirteen!! Imagine having friends like that??? Then there is Dorian and Chaol who literally see and refer to themselves as brothers<br /><br /><b> What I didn’t like </b><br /><br />- This book was just too long. There was a point where I just wanted it to be over. I feel like the war parts could have been reduced because most of those sections weren’t needed tbh. Also, there were too many characters and they all had their mini-plots. I couldn’t even remember alot of them and I had to google some of the names. Like who in Ansel? The silent assassins? The people from Suria etc. I didn’t care about alot of characters bc I didn’t really know them<br /><br />- Some parts were just corny especially regarding Aelin <br /><br />- This book should have done a better just at summarizing some plots that happened in previous books as a way to refreshen our memory. Like I remembered nothing about the 'nameless' situation<br /><br /><b> Some confusing parts </b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Why can Dorian shapeshift? Why did Maeve kill connall as a way to punish Aelin when they weren’t even friends?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall, I was satisfied with the way things concluded and I’m going to miss reading about my faves 😪<br /><br /><br /><b> Pre-reading Update </b><br />I just read the mini-excerpt of this and although I'm not the biggest fan of the two Main characters, it did touch my heart 😭😭😭 Can't wait until October!!!<br /><br />******<br />Hopefully, Dorian shines in this. His weak portrayal isn't cute!! 😒</span>
  <a data-text-id="9168298681062243723" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1736956640" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18254417710810205154"><i>”Once upon a time, in a land long since burned to ash, there lived a young princess who loved her Kingdom…”</i><br/><br/>I honestly loved the final book in series, however I’m going to start off by saying this is nowhere near perfect, I picked up on a lot of things during my read but I’ll get into that later. However as a whole I thoroughly enjoyed the final instalment to the Throne of Glass Series, I can’t believe it’s officially over. After going over my thoughts and feelings weighing up the likes and disli</span>
  <span id="freeText18254417710810205154" style="display:none"><i>”Once upon a time, in a land long since burned to ash, there lived a young princess who loved her Kingdom…”</i><br /><br />I honestly loved the final book in series, however I’m going to start off by saying this is nowhere near perfect, I picked up on a lot of things during my read but I’ll get into that later. However as a whole I thoroughly enjoyed the final instalment to the Throne of Glass Series, I can’t believe it’s officially over. After going over my thoughts and feelings weighing up the likes and dislikes I can’t give it all of the stars that I originally did, but there are so many reasons as to why. Just a pre warning I've marked off where <b>spoilers</b> begin so please keep that in mind.<br /><br />Going into this, I was seriously worried, there are so many characters that I became seriously attached to so going into this with the full expectation that they were going to a war, not only that but seen as though it’s the FINAL book, I was very curious to find out what would finally happen and would it meet my expectations.<br /><br />This is not a small book <b>980 pages!</b> I mean it’s a whopper to say the least, so when it’s this big I kind of want EVERYTHING, and it does give you a lot, however some of it to me seemed to be slightly filler scenes that didn’t add anything to the story and was there just for the sake of it. The first section of the book I was so hooked, it was brutal and heart wrenching and we really got to see a lot more of Fenrys and how his and Aelins friendship built up over a traumatic few months.<br /><br />Honestly, I think I faced every form of emotion in this book, I cried with happiness, absolute bawled my eyes out (full on ugly crying and closing the book because nope), laughed, cried some more. It was an absolute rollercoaster. <br /><br /><b>Just to warn you I go into detail about things from this point on, so if you don’t want to read <u>spoilers</u> please don’t continue.</b><br /><br /><u>Characters</u><br /><br /><i>”It is the strength of this that matters. No matter where you are, no matter how far, this will lead you home.”</i><br /><br />So I can strongly say that I have a love hate relationship with <b>Aelin and Rowan</b>, and this is still the case. Aelin goes through hell and back for a long part of this book and seeing her go into herself was so sad to see, but her strength was unyielding and even though she isn’t my favourite character I can honestly say that I respected her so much more. The thing that irritates me though is that at times, I found it very very frustrating that she didn’t seem to believe Dorian was capable of doing things. Then we have Rowan, I don’t really know what to say, the whole claiming part is very off putting, I don’t have a lot to say to be honest I think you either like him, or you don’t and he’s meh for me. I'm not really sure what he brought to this...<br /><br />I’m not sure how to word this. I love <i>Chaol and Yerene</i>, especially after Tower of Dawn, and I went from a full book about these two, to kind of not enough. I mean we had a bit, but I needed <u>more</u>! It was so lovely to see how fare they’d both come. They love they have for each other and the protectiveness they feel. I adored how Chaol let Serene decide things for herself (as it should be) but from what he once was to this we finally got the Chaol back that we all (or some of us) know and love. I loved the friendships that Yerene made with the other characters especially Elide. <br /><br /><b>Manon and Dorian</b> are my ultimate favourites of this series, and they both brought so much to these series independently and together. Together, the closeness they have and that they allow themselves to be open and honest and as time goes on that becomes so much more apparent, along with the bickering I was here for it. Manon alone is such a strong female character, she’s a true leader and it was interesting to see her step up to her role. I was crying when she became Queen and she deserves every one of them stars atop her head! Her love for the thirteen and Abraxos are so hear wrenching, and the further you go in to the story you see her become more and more aware of what she wants. Dorian was such an interesting character in this book, learning more about his powers and what he was able to achieve and learn. He played the game and did it so cleverly, and not only that, but learning about his father and his name. My HEART!<br /><br /> <i>The Thirteen and Abraxos</i> are EVERYTHING! From the moment I met them I knew these were the characters I needed in this series. The strength and unity they show. In Particular Asterin forever having Manons back, when it came to the speeches and she was just so brave! Then of course Abraxos, my god. The absolute <b>fear</b> I had for him. I never knew I could feel so protective over a mythical creature but here we are!<br /> <br /><i>”I will always find you”</i><br /><br />I didn’t know where things would pick off with <b>Elide and Lorcan</b> I was curious to see what would happen between the two, although things started off not the best it was so GOOD to see them together. One of my favourite chapters in the book was when Elide went to Save Lorcan, my god, it was intense and heart stopping but it was <u>everything</u>. I cannot get over Lorcans new name, I’m laughing just thinking about it. But I love a salty character, and Lorcan is 100% that!<br /><br /><i>Fenrys and Gavriel</i> <b>Blink Once</b> My god. I never knew how much I would come to love Fenrys, I really didn’t but he was such a <u>highlight</u> for me in this book, I can’t even begin to explain without going into a full on gush about his character. I love him. The end. I feel so sad for Gavriel, there could be so much to said, but I don’t think he was in it enough which is a shame.<br /><br /><i>”But just remember that this fear of yours? It means you have something worth fighting for something you care so greatly for that losing it is the worst thing you can imagine”</i><br /><br />Where to begin with <b>Lysandra and Aedion</b>. Firstly out of all of the POVs, these were my least favourite, at times I found the scenes to be slightly repetitive and at times I strongly disliked Aedion, I just found him to be childish, but as the story progressed I can put my hand in the air and say that he actually grew on me, I’m still quite shocked but he honestly did. He remained so strong even when everything went to shit and he finally admitted how he felt which I was very happy about. Then there’s Lysandra once again another strong female character, the courage she has and the never ending sacrifices she made throughout. I’ve always liked Lysandra and her ability, but seeing how much she could do. I loved it!<br /><br /><i>Nesryn and Sartaq</i>, in a book this big, they were barely mentioned, it honestly seemed like the birds were mentioned more with how beautiful they were, I loved them BOTH in Tower of Dawn and to see them barely in it. However Empress sounds good I guess?<br /><br />Then we have <b>Erawan and Maeve</b>. I live for an evil character, and multiple times throughout this I honestly thought Maeve was going to get a redemption arc, and I was thinking Not Today Satan, Not Today. It was interesting to see Maeves thought process and how she dealt with things, then Erawen was a bit I don’t know meh? I’m kind of miffed at how they both came to an end, I mean I liked that it wasn’t just Aelin being like I DID IT ALL, so that’s a plus.<br /><br />A few extra shout outs; <br /><br />Evangeline and Darrow a very unexpected thing but I liked it!<br />Falkan… once again, not really there, but what I saw of him I liked.<br />Murtaugh, awwww<br /><br /><i>”Live”</i><br /><br />What I <b>liked?</b><br /><br />- We got to see NOX again! I loved him in Throne of Glass and I’d missed him so much, and to learn he’d been a spy in the first book I was like GURL, however does anyone know what happened to him, or is this just me that last saw him plodding along to send for aid?<br />- <b>Witches!</b> As we all know by now, Manon is a babe. It was just SO GOOD seeing her bring everyone together and honestly I can hand on my heart say I legit cried with how proud I was of her when she brought them all together, such a feel good moment.<br />- My mind seemed to be merging the books together and probably forgetting things from previous books, but Dorians sword was everything, and also another thing I may of missed previously from other books, or just don’t remember was the use of the spiders and that they can shape shift as well was very clever. <br />- How much everyone disliked Chaol father, it just felt so fitting and Yerene telling him off was something else<br />- The revenge on Cairn, like I’m not one for violence, but he was such an awful awful character<br />- The codes between Aelin and Fenrys, at there darkest time they still found a way to communicate and continued to do so throughout.<br />- BABY TOWERS, I need this in my life and I didn’t even know.<br />- ALL OF THE REUNITING, I was a blubbering mess for all of them, I was so happy especially with Dorian and Chaol, my heart couldn’t take it. <br />- All of the <b>tension</b> and building up to what was going to come<br />- Those letters, I can’t<br />- It’s pretty apparent that Aeidon is not my favourite character, however his talk with Evangeline was literally everything and once again I teared up, how can I not?!<br />- Hello Rhys and Feyre<br />- The Sword and Shield situation<br />- Blood Oaths, the final two DESTROYED me<br />- The tattoos also destroyed me. I swear I cried for the last 6% of the book for no reason other than how emotional I was with everything that had happened.<br /><br />What I <b>didn’t like</b>?<br /><br />- This is the one thing that really irked me throughout, the timings seem to be so all over the place, it is lead to believe that this takes place just over a year since Throne of Glass, but I’ve discussed this with numerous people and none of us can seem to work it out. So if you have <b>any idea</b> please let me know because I am beyond confused.<br />- In some relationships I know we all say things we don’t always mean, but there are <u>two</u> cases of this where it kind of goes too far with me. There is one with Aedion and Lysandra, he throws her out of his tent in anger and disgust and says some very hurtful things yet when she is near death he suddenly tells her how much he loves her etc. like in any common sense I don’t understand how this is normal? Then we have Elide and Lorcan, don’t get me wrong I love <u>both</u> of these, but Elide does the same to Lorcan and then when it happens to him the same thing happens. <br />- This is a <b>war</b> there are always going to be casualties I get that, but there are only two significant deaths and both left me feeling very very bitter. The first is that not ONE of the Thirteen survived other than Manon. It honestly threw me for loop. It annoys me that everyone seemed to get a happy ending other than Manon who literally lost everyone other than Abraxos, and even then HE LOST HIS MATE! Then we have Gavriel, he literally sees Aedion and they re-connect (but not really) and then low and behold <b>one page later</b> yes one, he’s dead. Just meh! So on top of this, no one else dies, in a war where there are so many deaths. I just don’t get it.<br />- While reading this, there are SO many similarities to Lord of the Rings, once you notice it, you can’t un-see it. I understand this is a fantasy book and things are going to cross over but some things are so un-canny it’s hard not to notice.<br />- The rep in this book. How many characters do we have? They are all male and female relationships, the “leading” characters are prominently white. Anyone with a bit of Diversity isn’t really seen as much in the book which is disappointing.<br />- Finally I really did enjoy the end don’t get me wrong BUT I wish we’d of seen more of the other characters, Manon is legit my Queen, my favourite character out of the whole series and how she leaves was just so poor and unsatisfying, and then the others were a kind of cya later type thing. I know that it would of been longer but it was just something I’d of enjoyed.<br /><br />Overall I really really did enjoy this book, as I mentioned it’s not perfect, but the series as a whole was brought to a very enjoyable end. It was a great end to the series, it had all of the feels, and I’m probably going to be in a major book hangover, but it’s the price you pay. Now if you want to give me a spin off with Manon and Dorian that would be delightful.<br /><br /><i>”A better world.”</i><br /><br />Re-Read 17.12.19<br /><br />I’ve knocked this down a star, I just. Some of this makes me so mad...<br /><br />Okay here I go!<br /><br />Some spoilers ahead...<br /><br />In the things I don’t like these issues just stood out to me more and more. It really really frustrates me how badly Dorian and Manon was treated in this book. <br /><br />I just feel like the sun shines out of Aelins arse and Dorian is just a side note when really it’s on BOTH of them and Dorian is just as powerful! Then everything that happened with Manon the injustice of it all. Everyone got their “happy ending” I mean come on.<br /><br />It genuinely felt like I was watching the last season of GoT this time around, going in I knew what to expect however this is a war, and I think that sacrifices have to be made with some “big” characters have to die not just the “side characters” and I know it’s heartbreaking but these things need to be done to show the impact of what’s actually happened.<br /><br />The characters I love in this series were kind of pushed aside and it just irks me at how “perfect” everything ended up. I am not here for it, I’m salty and I’m bitter. There I said it!<br /><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1493562017?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne of Glass</a> - 5 Stars<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1644462199?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Crown of Midnight</a> - 5 Stars<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1644462208?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Heir of Fire</a> - 4 Stars<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1493560617?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Queen of Shadows</a> - 4 Stars<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1592872177?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Empire of Storms</a> - 5 Stars<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2143674805?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Tower of Dawn</a> - 5 Stars<br />Kingdom of Ash - 4 Stars<br />-----------<br />After finishing the book ramble...<br /><b>ALL OF THE STARS!</b><br /><br />It's done. I am emotionally drained. I laughed, I cried, I went through every emotion.<br />Well done for everyone who made it, we did it!<br /><br /><i>Full RTC</i><br /><br />---------<br /><b>20.05.2018</b><br />Over 1000 pages, give it all to me.<br /><br />I need everything Manon and Dorian related.<br />Thanksssss<br />————<br />12.07.2018<br />I'm in love with the UK cover, the gods have blessed us!<br />————</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Yy7CnySila7VbB84mlwy5EOLVsAXceQsNGWsOo2bttIB6LJDCuxw10pPyS2v6MFaBZ0HUKwcPv/WvhbK9X9w3g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2AwejqydLUomSlclnAffiBkaAWWTAj6gxvkFUSnmeL26ym5SgtPIM7lpgTCpsyw2XwxQ9Shv5HMkIr+hUQK+sQ==')})
  }
//]]>

He may have taken her, but he will never have her.\n\nA Choice...\n\nCasteel Da’Neer is known by many names and many faces. His lies are as seductive as his touch. His truths as sensual as his bite. Poppy knows better than to trust him. He needs her alive, healthy, and whole to achieve his goals. But he’s the only way for her to get what she wants—to find her brother Ian and see for herself if he has become a soulless Ascended. Working with Casteel instead of against him presents its own risks. He still tempts her with every breath, offering up all she’s ever wanted. Casteel has plans for her. Ones that could expose her to unimaginable pleasure and unfathomable pain. Plans that will force her to look beyond everything she thought she knew about herself—about him. Plans that could bind their lives together in unexpected ways that neither kingdom is prepared for.
